  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_834a4945-a00a-4512-aaba-a2fc5bea4375'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4478473197476036695" style="display:none"><i>Plagued by a war between magic and technology, Atlanta has never been so deadly. Good thing Kate Daniels is on the job.</i><br /><br />Kate Daniels may have quit the Order of Merciful Aid, but she’s still knee-deep in paranormal problems. Or she would be if she could get someone to hire her. Starting her own business has been more challenging than she thought it would be—now that the Order is disparaging her good name, and many potential clients are afraid of getting on the bad side of the Beast Lord, who just happens to be Kate’s mate.<br /><br />So when Atlanta’s premier Master of the Dead calls to ask for help with a vampire on the loose, Kate leaps at the chance of some paying work. Turns out this is not an isolated incident, and Kate needs to get to the bottom of it—fast, or the city and everyone dear to her might pay the ultimate price.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_139241495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139241495" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139241495?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139241495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15975527785975492713">*Before I begin my review, I must take a moment to honour the devastating goddess who made it possible for me to read this book. There are not enough words in the English language to fully capture the incadescents of this magnificent human being. She is beyond reproach, loved by all, exulted in her graciousness. I adore her with the nuclear reactions of a thousand suns. She is worth more to me than all of the precious jewels!*<br/><br/>/Suck up<br/><br/>"The series gets good at book three."<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380343666ra/698970.gif' alt='Neil Patrick Harris pretending to shoot himself' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If I had a penny for ever</span>
  <span id="freeText15975527785975492713" style="display:none">*Before I begin my review, I must take a moment to honour the devastating goddess who made it possible for me to read this book. There are not enough words in the English language to fully capture the incadescents of this magnificent human being. She is beyond reproach, loved by all, exulted in her graciousness. I adore her with the nuclear reactions of a thousand suns. She is worth more to me than all of the precious jewels!*<br><br>/Suck up<br><br>"The series gets good at book three."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380343666ra/698970.gif" alt="Neil Patrick Harris pretending to shoot himself" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I had a penny for every time I heard something like this about a series then... okay, I'd probably have about a dollar now.<br><br>But still, for many avid readers out there, it is the bane of their existence. <br><br>No, but really. This series gets GOOD at book three.<br><br>Unlike most people though, I didn't mind it at book one. I thought it had a lot of potential. Some people get thrown off of being tossed into an unfamiliar world with little or no hand-holding from the author. Note: Ilona Andrews will never hold your hand. You either keep up or she'll leave you behind.<br><br>For me the second book was an improvement but still only representative of a slightly better-than-average series. <br><br>Then the third book happened. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343666i/698971.jpg" alt="huge explosion" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>It really, really happened...</i><br><br>Ever since then, I've been in love with Kate Daniels, Ilona Andrews, and her Edge series. <br><br>Magic Slays lives up to the series fairly well.<br><br>It's intelligent, witty, well-paced, fun, easy to read and enjoyable. <br><br>The character arcs are all interesting, realistic, involving and enjoyable.<br><br>My only complaint with this series is that Andrews is obviously very uncomfortable about any intimate scenes. She has the writer's equivalent of premature ejaculation and at one point I almost wanted to stroke the book and mutter, "It's okay. Really. It is. It happens to everyone."<br><br>Andrews, like Neil and unlike most of the Urban Fantasy authors, actually seems to LIKE women. The friendship between Kate and Andrea, her ward Julie and her dealings with the other women in this book is so well treated! It's a breath of fresh air to have a female protagonist who actually gets along with other women.<br><br>Over all, if you're a fan of this series, definitely read the latest installment.<br><br>If you're not a fan of this series - please don't shoot me but...<br><br>It gets good at book three.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15975527785975492713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578642175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13308938984749331228"><b>
  <u>Welcome to the Reader’s Court of Literary Grievances</u>
</b><br/><br/>The courtroom was alive with the buzz of conversation. Today’s case had drawn so many spectators that it was standing room only. Behind the judge’s bench, high on the wall, hung an unimposing, standard-issue clock. As its hands ticked down the minutes, the excitement in the room rose and the buzz of the crowd slowly turned into a low level roar. <br/><br/>Fifteen minutes before start-time it was so loud that people had to raise their voices when spea</span>
  <span id="freeText13308938984749331228" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Welcome to the Reader’s Court of Literary Grievances</u>
</b><br /><br />The courtroom was alive with the buzz of conversation. Today’s case had drawn so many spectators that it was standing room only. Behind the judge’s bench, high on the wall, hung an unimposing, standard-issue clock. As its hands ticked down the minutes, the excitement in the room rose and the buzz of the crowd slowly turned into a low level roar. <br /><br />Fifteen minutes before start-time it was so loud that people had to raise their voices when speaking to their neighbors or risk losing their words to the cacophony that reverberated around them. Every now and then shouting could be heard ringing out over the din, another die-hard fangirl losing their temper in one of the many heated debates that were taking place.<br /><br />“How can you even say that?!” one woman screamed. “Anita Blake could wipe the floor with Mercy Thompson.”<br /><br />“Oh yeah?” another chorused. “Well Rachel Morgan is a <i>demon</i>. She could drag Anita into the ever after and leave her there to rot!”<br /><br />“She’d just screw her way out!” yet another joined in.<br /><br />And so it continued. At one point a scuffle even broke out near the rear doors but luckily it was quickly broken up before it could escalate into a full blown brawl. With the energy level of the room hovering around frenetic, all it would take was one stray punch for the crowd to implode. <br /><br />At precisely three o’clock, a door on the empty side of the bar swung open and those assembled began to fall silent. The first person to appear was the bailiff, a towering man with cold, dark eyes that scanned the crowd as he moved towards his post. Following him were the court clerk, the court reporter and finally, swathed in billowing black robes, the judge. He was not what most of the spectators expected. He was…young. He was handsome too, with broad shoulders, dark hair cut close to his head and gray eyes that seemed to glow with some sort of inner power. Those eyes swept the crowd much as the bailiff’s had and the individuals they fell upon seemed to cower beneath his gaze. <br /><br />Once he was fully ensconced behind the bench, more people filed in through the side door. These were dressed in expensive looking suits and seemed to wear similar expressions on their faces; a mix of supreme confidence and utter boredom. Only the thin bands of sweat on their upper lips or the nervous twitching of a hand gave away their true feelings. As much as they’d like to pretend otherwise, this was not just another court case. <br /><br />These new arrivals took their seats behind the two desks that faced the judge and began to open briefcases and shuffle through papers as they talked amongst themselves. Behind them, the crowd was so quiet you could hear a pin drop. It was as though the collective was holding its breath for something. <br /><br />The last person to enter the room was a woman of medium height and medium build with light brown hair pulled back off her face. This was clearly what the crowd had been waiting for. As soon as they caught sight of her, they erupted, some hurling angry words and threats and others rising up to shout them down in between cheering her as she sauntered over to her seat, a smirk splitting her face. <br /><br />“Order! Order!” the judge roared, his deep voice echoing throughout the marble and stone room so that it seemed he’d spoken the words three times. Something in his tone brooked no argument and the crowd fell into a low level grumbling and then finally back into silence. Those who snuck glances at him quickly looked away, unnerved by the way his eyes seemed to flash under the electric lights. <br /><br />Taking advantage of the moment, the bailiff stepped forward and spoke into the hush. “Today we’re here to rule on The People versus Navessa in the Case of the Most Badass Heroine.”<br /><br />And so it began. It was the trial they’d been waiting for, the one that would decide it all. Navessa's case was a good one and her lawyers well versed in both Urban Fantasy and Paranormal Romance. They knew the standards, knew the tropes and the themes and they’d spent months preparing for this. Preparing to prove, once and for all, that Kate Daniels was the most badass main character to ever grace the pages of a book.<br /><br />The prosecution was equally stacked. Among their papers were innumerable quotes spoken by the many heroines that made up their client list. They had weapon inventories, outfit inventories and even in one case…a boyfriend inventory. They had pages and pages of descriptive paragraphs detailing fight scenes, magical badassery, heartbreak and heroism. It would be a tough trial. <br /><br />“Will the prosecution please begin its opening statement,” the bailiff ordered.<br /><br />In response, a tall man with thinning grey hair moved sinuously up out of his seat and strode towards the center of the room, placing himself in full view of both the judge and the crowd. He turned towards his audience with a smile that could have sold souls to the devil himself. <br /><br />“My job is not to disprove Kate Daniels being a badass,” he began. <br /><br />From her seat behind the defense table, Navessa watched him like a hawk. As he continued to speak, his low, soothing voice ringing out through the room, she realized he was good. He was really good. Listening to him wax poetic about the preponderance of evidence and the impossibility of decisively placing a single character above all others would have made almost anyone nervous. <br /><br />Not her. You see, she knew every single one of his clients. Had known them for years in fact. She knew their dirty little secrets, their hidden agendas and most importantly, their weaknesses. And she and her lawyers were prepared to use it all against them. <br /><br />When the prosecutor was done with his statement, the head of her defense stood and strode to the same spot that her enemy had just occupied. Navessa knew the speech she was about to deliver by heart, she’d helped write it. <br /><br />“Kate Daniels, is a badass. This is irrefutable,” her lawyer began. For the next three minutes she laid out their case in broad terms, citing numerous sources to include sales statistics, critical reviews and ratings on book related websites. It was a good speech and the crowd, which had started whispering almost the moment she opened her mouth, slowly fell silent over the course of it. By the end more than a few were nodding along in agreement. <br /><br />The trial lasted three days. Evidence was submitted and poured over in excruciating detail, experts were brought in followed by critics. At the end of the second day a psychologist even spoke, and he seemed to think everyone involved in the trial was in dire need of his services. On the final day, it was the witnesses’ turns. It was these men and women that made the case electric, emotional and absolutely unpredictable. One woman, called to the stand <i>for</i> the prosecution, broke down in tears halfway through questioning by the defense. <br /><br />“I just don’t understand why she had to sleep with so many men the way she did. I would have been fine if she had just owned up to her behavior but nooooo, she blamed it on the Ardeur. I <i>hate</i> her now!” she sobbed.<br /><br />“I understand,” Navessa's lawyer smiled kindly, barely masking the predatory gleam in her eye. And therein lay the genius of their defense. For who hadn’t been irritated at one point or another while reading about their favorite heroines? Who hadn’t thought they’d acted too-stupid-to-live? Who wasn’t still angry about it on some level? What Navessa knew was that the number of times she’d felt this way about Kate Daniels was a fraction of a fraction of the number she had for the prosecution’s clients. She knew that the amount of other readers that felt this same way might very well win them this case and so her lawyers were vicious in their cross examination of the witnesses. <br /><br />Closing arguments took place at the end of the third day. The same snake of a man that gave the opening statement for the prosecution spoke again, addressing the judge this time, instead of the crowd. There was no jury here today; the decision would come down to the imposing man that had ruled over the past days of proceedings with a solemn face and a quiet dignity. <br /><br />“Your honor,” he began. “Has the defense proven beyond a reasonable doubt that Kate Daniels is the most badass of the badass?” <br /><br />Navessa had to stifle her urge to snort. She listened along with the crowd as this man rehashed all the evidence that supported not that one of his clients was <i>more</i> badass than Kate but that the defense had failed to prove that Kate was the <i>most</i> badass. <br /><br />When he was finished a few people in the crowd even clapped and for the first time Navessa felt a stab of worry. But then her lawyer was standing from her chair, striding confidently to the center of the room. She turned not to face the judge, but the crowd. <br /><br />“We’ve all been together in this room the last three days. We know what’s taken place. We know that there <b>is</b> one character that reigns supreme over all others and we know that her name is Kate Daniels so in closing I’d like to site just one more quote and it’s the quote heard round the paranormal world. The one that made us arch an eyebrow, crack a smile. It’s the one that alluded to there being a new badass in town and that she was everything we’d been wishing for.” Here she paused for dramatic effect and Navessa's eyes swept out over the crowd. They were on the edge of their seats, their faces rapt as they waited for her lawyer to speak again. Finally she did, whispering in a low, sing song voice <i>“Here, kitty, kitty, kitty.”</i><br /><br />No sooner had she taken her seat than the javelin dropped. “The court rules in favor of the defendant,” the judge spoke in the same monotone he’d been using the past three days. The courtroom erupted in reaction, the prosecution shooting to their feet to protest, the crowd behind them mostly cheering but with pockets contention erupting here and there. <br /><br />As her lawyers shook hands and patted each other on the back, Navessa turned away and pretended to pack up some papers, her eyes straying to the judge as he gathered himself to leave. Beneath her breath, so quiet that someone standing next to her wouldn’t even be able to hear the words, she whispered “Nice dye job, Your Majesty.” The judge turned to go as though he had all the time in the world but Navessa could have sworn she caught the hint of a smile playing upon his lips.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13308938984749331228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <i>“Put your badass faces on and follow me.” </i>

</blockquote><br>Kate Daniels is now the Beast Lord's mate and she has her own business that investigates paranormal problems and life would be perfect,if only someone hired her.And her ward stopped escaping from her private school.And she wasn't afraid that her father would finally come to kill her.And a device of disastrous potential that threatened Atlanta's citizens was found.And an underground organisation didn't try to murder her.A humble mercenary's life is never perfect after all.<br><br><b>
  <u>Confessions of a Kate Daniels addict</u>
</b><br><b>1.Addicted to action.</b>While reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8559047.Magic_Slays__Kate_Daniels___5_" title="Magic Slays (Kate Daniels, #5) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Slays</a> I wasn't sure whether I would give it 4 or 5 stars.Of course <b>I loved it</b>,but <b>I didn't find it as intense as the previous ones</b>.And then the final pages happened and <b>battles</b> and <b>bombs</b> and <b>ancient rituals</b> and <b>massacres</b> occured and everything fell into place.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450366390ra/17416785.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>2.Addicted to sarcasm.</b>Sarcasm here,sarcasm there,sarcasm <b>everywhere</b>!Kate is the queen but every single character has a witty retort ready to strike and make you <b>snicker</b> until you sound like Squidward Tentacles.It's not pleasant for the people around you but don't be ashamed,things could always get worse! (I can't find an example to support my case but I blame the sleep deprivation,I'm sure you can think of something more embarassing than sounding like a grumpy cartoon)<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What do you mean fainted?<br>Took a dive, kissed the pavement. Swooned like a southern belle after her first kiss. Had a dreadful case of the vapors.” </i>
  </b>

  <b>

  </b>

You would take care of me, because you love me. I love you too, Kate. If you ever became hurt, I would not leave you.<br>I’ll be there. Wherever you want‘there’ to be.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450369335ra/17417166.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ok I admit,it was this exact scene that convinced me to give the fifth star.Curran and Kate are one of my all time favorite couples,they make me swoon with declarations like this,they have hot sex that makes me blush and then they fight and kick each other in the head without regrets.Kate is still an insubordinate pigheaded ass,Curran is still a manipulative control freak,but they manage to stay together despite their differences because that's what we call <b>love</b>.<br><br>The time has come to return to the real world with the exams and the essays,but I can proudly claim that no matter how many times Gandalf said<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450369335ra/17417167.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I ignored him and dedicated a few hours to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8559047.Magic_Slays__Kate_Daniels___5_" title="Magic Slays (Kate Daniels, #5) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Slays</a>.I hope the book gods will help their faithful servant.</span>

<div id="review_143750597" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143750597" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143750597?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=with-smut">with-smut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=uf-or-pnr">uf-or-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143750597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7479984916308056966">I would like all authors of urban fantasy and paranormal romance out there to stop for a second their feverish scribbling and take a look at this series. THE proof that YES, series don't necessarily need to go down the drain after 4th installment, that YES, series can STILL be interesting after the two romantic interests in the story "do the deed" and that YES, plots do not need to become unbelievably twisted, punctuated by improbable events and where mythology gets slaughtered just to get out o</span>
  <span id="freeText7479984916308056966" style="display:none">I would like all authors of urban fantasy and paranormal romance out there to stop for a second their feverish scribbling and take a look at this series. THE proof that YES, series don't necessarily need to go down the drain after 4th installment, that YES, series can STILL be interesting after the two romantic interests in the story "do the deed" and that YES, plots do not need to become unbelievably twisted, punctuated by improbable events and where mythology gets slaughtered just to get out of the bloody unplanned mess that became your story's outline.<br /><br />Now, instead of giving you a synopsis of the book, I'd rather tell you why this book in particular, but the whole series in general, deserved 5 stars:<br /><br />- because the plot is interesting, well developed, makes total sense, each book is tied to the other but still stands on its own without painful, mean and useless cliffhangers;<br /><br />- because romance in this book is not the vital core of the story but rather like a planet orbiting around a much substantial and well-founded plot - so much so that in the first book there is NO romance and we're still all here, inhaling every single word Andrews is writing;<br /><br />- because vampires, in these books, do not sparkle;<br /><br />- because the Andrews, when they decided to put mythology into their world, did their homework well and decided to stick with what they knew: in this book, they stuck with Russian mythology and used it in a great, clever way - there is no Russian kid who hasn't heard of Baba Yaga that I'm aware of;<br /><br />-because Kate is simply and undeniably the baddest UF heroine out there at the moment; she is clever, disillusioned, snarky and she kicks ass so much that I wish I was her;<br /><br />-because the dialogue is so full of snark, banter, sarcasm and great comebacks that I am SURE everybody has highlighted some part or the other of the book;<br /><br />Finally, the main reason why I think this series is so fortunate: because the Andrews are two. So what? Even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17015.P_C__Cast" title="P.C. Cast" rel="nofollow noopener">P.C. Cast</a> are two. No. I think the fact that a man and a woman have written this series together has given it a great balance. Thanks to Gordon Andrews being present, the books never get cheesy, overly romantic or dangerously stupid. On the contrary, you can see where he puts in his knowledge of weapons, fighting strategies and so on. He gives the books a masculine angle that only helps making Kate even more of a badass. The fact that the authors are husband and wife shows in the dialogues between Kate and Curran, I think.<br /><br />In all this awesomeness, I am not saying that the book - or the series - is perfect. There are flaws: some that have to do with proofreading - a "door bursts open" immediately after having fallen into the room - some with the plot - I think there is a certain confusion at times about the form the beasts take, half form, warrior form, full animal. There is a passage where Mahon shouldn't have been able to shift into warrior form yet he does - and some have to do with excessive detailing - those who followed and understood the whole coefficient and proportion thing about probability of loupism please raise your hand. Also, I was pretty sorry that Raphael was not in this book, and I expect him in the next one.<br />Still, somehow, these imperfections do not detract from the general state of satisfaction I was left in after I read the last page of the book. <br /><br />Dear Ilona and Gordon Andrews, if you keep on writing like this, I will gladly buy Magic Whatever # 15.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7479984916308056966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-go-girl-kickass-heroine">you-go-girl-kickass-heroine</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254890978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17901716865340179968">My massive 2018 overdose of Kate Daniels continues with <i>Magic Slays</i>, the fifth book in the series. Kate is starting up her own private investigation business, which isn’t initially going so great (in fact, they have no clients at all), and she’s trying to come to terms with her relationship with Curran and her new role as the <s>First Lady</s> <s>Mate</s> Consort to the Beast Master. <br/><br/>Kate has some angst about both of those things, but it soon gets overshadowed by a particularly difficult, and dangerous, case </span>
  <span id="freeText17901716865340179968" style="display:none">My massive 2018 overdose of Kate Daniels continues with <i>Magic Slays</i>, the fifth book in the series. Kate is starting up her own private investigation business, which isn’t initially going so great (in fact, they have no clients at all), and she’s trying to come to terms with her relationship with Curran and her new role as the <s>First Lady</s> <s>Mate</s> Consort to the Beast Master. <br /><br />Kate has some angst about both of those things, but it soon gets overshadowed by a particularly difficult, and dangerous, case that Kate is offered. What do uncontrolled vampires on the loose and a disappearing inventor have to do with each other? And can Kate solve the case and avoid getting herself and her loved ones killed in the process? It's especially difficult when her ward, Julie, absconds from the private school where Kate had sent her and makes her way back to Kate, and danger, and Curran has major issues every time Kate walks into peril … or too close to another man.<br /><br />As usual with books in the KATE DANIELS series, you get lots of ass-kicking, sarcastic dialogue, conflicts and makeup scenes with His Royal Furriness, and freaky dangers - and this is a good one. The plot was a tense one, even if the ultimate bad guys didn't strike me as particularly believable<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, and yes, I realize it's strange to think that weird exotic monsters are <b>so much more</b> plausible than a group of non-magic people who are willing to commit mass murder to eradicate magic from the world again <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But that's really my only major complaint here. </span>

<div id="review_351591269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351591269" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351591269?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11055258-magic-slays">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The WHOLE world.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=southern-comfort">southern-comfort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=weres-shapeshifters">weres-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dead-things">dead-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=creeptastic">creeptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351591269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2926098149810754441"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>At the end of Kate #4, Curran sets Kate up in her own business. CALM DOWN. He doesn't just give it to her, it's a <i>business</i> arrangement. One that will ultimately benefit both Kate AND the Pack. <br/><br/>But having her own business does Kate not one bit of good, b/c that bigoted jackhole Ted, her ex-bossman from the Order, tried to blame the epic disaster that his "plan" to take out Erra devolved into on Kate. Anyone with a lick of sense knows that's not true, but come on . . . how much sense does</span>
  <span id="freeText2926098149810754441" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />At the end of Kate #4, Curran sets Kate up in her own business. CALM DOWN. He doesn't just give it to her, it's a <i>business</i> arrangement. One that will ultimately benefit both Kate AND the Pack. <br /><br />But having her own business does Kate not one bit of good, b/c that bigoted jackhole Ted, her ex-bossman from the Order, tried to blame the epic disaster that his "plan" to take out Erra devolved into on Kate. Anyone with a lick of sense knows that's not true, but come on . . . how much sense does the general population typically have?&lt;-----NOT much.<br /><br />So Kate sits around in her empty office building, staring at the phone, willing it to ring, and when does, it's Ghastek . . . <br /><br />One of his journeyman necromancers lost control of a vampire, you see. It's headed towards Kate, and some help, please? ALSO--try not to kill it.<br /><br />Kate captures the rogue vamp (b/c awesome), but the cops (PAD) show up anyway, and they're feeling trigger happy, which is Bad. B/c Ghastek, who has also shown up and retaken control of the vampire, passes out, loses control of the vamp <i>again</i>, and PAD starts shooting. And they're not shooting handguns with 8 or 12 bullets. NOPE. They are not. They're shooting some kind of machine gun that can (and did) cut a man in half, yes, <i>literally</i>, and can keep shooting a steady stream of ammo for nearly five minutes, by Kate's estimation. <br /><br />That's a lot of freaking bullets. <br /><br />So while the cops are distracted by the vamp distracted by the two halves of the formerly whole man, Kate drags Ghastek, a wounded journeyman, and a nearly catatonic third journeyman into her office, behind her very thick steel door. <br /><br />*bang bang* on the door.<br /><br /><b>Kate:</b> Yeah, what?<br /><br /><b>PAD:</b> Lemme in.<br /><br /><b>Kate:</b> Ha ha, you're funny.<br /><br /><b>PAD:</b> I'll bust your door down!<br /><br /><b>Andrea:</b> I don't think you will, and here's why:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"You can either get the paramedics in there or you can let another civilian die of their injuries, break into an office owned by the Pack, assault the Beast Lord's wife, and shoot a knight of the Order. You can do it either way, but I promise that if you somehow survive, twenty years from now, when you're old and broken, you'll look back at this moment and wish you had taken two seconds and thought about what you were doing, because this is the point where it all went very wrong."</i>
</blockquote><br />*waves at Andrea*<br /><br />So there's a lot of posturing, but ultimately, PAD backs down, EMTs grab Ghastek, etc., and Kate and Andrea are alone at last. Andrea tells Kate where she's been for the last month, and Kate offers her a job. <br /><br />One of the best parts of this book is the friendship that is Kate and Andrea. Not only are these two absolutely hilarious together, but the fact that Kate not only has a friend, but a friend she so obviously cares about, who cares about her in return . . . the FEELS, man, the FEELS. <br /><br />Kate is so far from the solitary merc we first met that you can't help but get a little emotional.<br /><br />So Kate and Andrea have only just formed their Kate and Andrea team when Rene (of Red Guard fame) shows up and offers them a job.<br /><br />And it all goes downhill from there. And by "downhill" I mean Very Bad Things are afoot. <br /><br />This installment of KATE DANIELS is awesome per usual. The only reason I didn't like it quite as much as books 3 and 4 was b/c less Kate History, and the Bad Guy wasn't connected to that history, so it was less personal. The premise though . . . pure awesomeness. And Kate History did play a significant role in resolving a situation that arose as a result of the Bad Guy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And who isn't 100% convinced that the voice/presence Kate felt when she was magicking Julie was Roland? B/c it totally was. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This was also a very emotional installment. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't even think Joey had been mentioned before this book. He was a total red shirt, but it didn't matter. When Jezabel lost it, so did I. I sat there boo-hooing, not understanding why I was boo-hooing, but boo-hooing nonetheless. And Ascanio tore me up too. Sitting in that loup cage, huddled around Julie, with ribs sticking out of his side. HE CARRIED HER UP THE STAIRS WITH TWO BROKEN LEGS. *wails* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Maybe it's b/c I've read these books so many times, but the Andrews have done a remarkable job of creating characters that feel real. This installment shows you what a lot of those characters are made of, and it makes you proud of them. PROUD. Of a fictional teenaged shifter who learns what it means to be part of the Pack. Proud of girl who was betrayed by the person she trusted the most and who dealt with that betrayal by learning to take care of herself. Proud of a woman who lost everything that mattered in her life but keeps on living.<br /><br />Seriously, if you haven't read these books already, get on that. Best. Series. EVER.<br /><br /><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136352204" rel="nofollow noopener">A Questionable Client (Kate Daniels, #0.5)</a>
</b><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351655149" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1)</a>
</b><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351650230" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2)</a>
</b><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351593191" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Strikes (Kate Daniels, #3)</a>
</b><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351710670" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Mourns (Kate Daniels, #3.5)</a>
</b><br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351592946" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bleeds (Kate Daniels, #4)</a>
</b><br /><b>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1806165929" />
    <a title="Sophia Triad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad"><img alt="Sophia Triad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591419108p2/44642860.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=wolves-lycans">wolves-lycans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=witches-wizards">witches-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=magic">magic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806165929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13360953220781587069">It is time for Kate to put her grown-up pants on and act like an adult. It is essential for her to deal with a number of things that need an adult attitude. So:<br/><br/>1.	For the first time, she has a business to run with employees and bills to pay. For a variety of reasons she keeps adding employees to her business and all these people have needs, i.e. better weapons, food, food and more food, extra chairs etc.<br/>She has to be cautious about her budget and her earnings, but I am not sure she is very succe</span>
  <span id="freeText13360953220781587069" style="display:none">It is time for Kate to put her grown-up pants on and act like an adult. It is essential for her to deal with a number of things that need an adult attitude. So:<br /><br />1.	For the first time, she has a business to run with employees and bills to pay. For a variety of reasons she keeps adding employees to her business and all these people have needs, i.e. better weapons, food, food and more food, extra chairs etc.<br />She has to be cautious about her budget and her earnings, but I am not sure she is very successful with this matter.<br /><br />2.	She is mated now. She needs to learn how to trust Curran and this is hard. She has learned from a young age that all males will eventually try to manipulate her and take advantage of her. Is Curran going to do the same? She is so suspicious and scared of this possibility, but her heart is telling her otherwise.<br />Curran is just Curran. Just adorable. There is a scene in which he gets mad and he tears up her cookbook. 5 minutes later, he just goes back to buy her another.<br /><br />3.	As the female Alpha of the Pack: she has to<br />•	obey rules and laws<br />•	follow protocol<br />•	have escorts and bodyguards<br />•	attend formal dinners<br />•	be the judge of conflicts between pack members and answer petitions<br />•	make decisions about other peoples’ lives and<br />•	think about the Pack first, naturally!<br /><br />Kate feels her choices are being taken from her. She needs to be careful every time in order not to cause a diplomatic episode or not to test Curran’s patient. Additionally, she is not sure if his Furriness is truly worried about her or if he is just a manipulative bastard.<br /><br />4.	She will learn the bitter, ugly, painful truth about her mother Kalina and her stepfather (Hint: Kate’s can also be called Katenga). And she will have to deal with it!<br /><br />5.	She is the guardian of a teenager. Not an easy job. Little Julie does not behave and she does not do what she is told. Kate has to learn to be a parent and to provide parental advice.<br /><br />6.	She has to come to terms with the fact that she will lose someone close to her. This is unacceptable for Kate. And I agree.<br /><br />7.	It is about time to embrace and practice her magic!<br /><br />A strange machine with unknown use and a secret anti-magic society are going to keep Kate and her friends on their toes and they will add complexity to the book.<br />Everyone who knows the secret just runs away and you have a constant feeling that the city is doomed. <br />There will be an excellent, epic battle with all the elite magic beings of Atlanta united against the common enemy. Pure awesomeness.<br /><br />I truly love how the relationship between Curran and Kate develops, how their emotions deepen and explanations are given about how much they mean to each other. <br />Kate is gradually maturing and transforming from a warrior girl in the first book to a woman in love who defends what is hers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13360953220781587069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11415604426367659161">Okay, this is easy. Since I'm a fanboy, it's super easy to write reviews because I can usually just do a gonzo.<br/><br/>Suffice to say, it's really fun to be getting into the characters. There might have been a little hiccup with Curran in this one... like there ain't hiccups in all of them... but it's nice to see the interplay.<br/><br/>I can't believe that Derek is actually growing on me, at long last. But Julie? Aww<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www'>www</a>.... pooooooor kid! This is definitely going to bite everyone in the butt. I know it.<br/><br/>Urban fan</span>
  <span id="freeText11415604426367659161" style="display:none">Okay, this is easy. Since I'm a fanboy, it's super easy to write reviews because I can usually just do a gonzo.<br /><br />Suffice to say, it's really fun to be getting into the characters. There might have been a little hiccup with Curran in this one... like there ain't hiccups in all of them... but it's nice to see the interplay.<br /><br />I can't believe that Derek is actually growing on me, at long last. But Julie? Aww<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www">www</a>.... pooooooor kid! This is definitely going to bite everyone in the butt. I know it.<br /><br />Urban fantasy, when done well like this, is really some of the most effortless reads out there. It gets rather special for me, though, when we get a who's who of mythology showing up, like Greek gods overcharging for body bags and large refrigerated units, or Baba Yaga giving cute little gifts to little girls. Hmmm.. wait... she has a tendency of doing that anyway... oh well. :)<br /><br />The switchover back to tech comes at a very nice time for me. I really wanted a good return to that world-building quirk, and I couldn't be happier. I love mad geniuses. :)<br /><br />And as always, great apocalyptic shit for the end. Total popcorn madness. :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5420248106134718007">Reread.<br/><br/>Again an enjoyable addition to the series. IA certainly knows how to spin a tale. It has its moments of fun and surprises but I think unlike the last this book seriously needed a great villain. IA just threw everything in the mix in this book i.e. vampire and shapeshifters going mad, a secret society who has it's minions in almost every big organisation in Atlanta giving this group all the inside scoop.<br/><br/>Despite my grumblings about the story, I loved Kate and Curran in this book. The things</span>
  <span id="freeText5420248106134718007" style="display:none">Reread.<br /><br />Again an enjoyable addition to the series. IA certainly knows how to spin a tale. It has its moments of fun and surprises but I think unlike the last this book seriously needed a great villain. IA just threw everything in the mix in this book i.e. vampire and shapeshifters going mad, a secret society who has it's minions in almost every big organisation in Atlanta giving this group all the inside scoop.<br /><br />Despite my grumblings about the story, I loved Kate and Curran in this book. The things she came to know about her past, her doubts about her future, and how Curran reacted to all that, that alone made this book worth reading. <br /><br />Now on to book 6. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9123918237605038137">4.5 stars.<br/>Ladies and Gentlemen, I believe we have a winner! Ilona and Andrew have done it again.<br/><br/>I have a plan to save urban fantasy. I’m not a megalomaniac or anything, I just think that UF needs saving and I care enough to try. Therefore, I’ve developed a cunning plan: I’m going to buy four more copies of this book. The first I’ll send to Jeanine Frost because she was the first of my favorite UF authors to disappoint me this year. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Hot wax? So not cool! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’ll send t</span>
  <span id="freeText9123918237605038137" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br />Ladies and Gentlemen, I believe we have a winner! Ilona and Andrew have done it again.<br /><br />I have a plan to save urban fantasy. I’m not a megalomaniac or anything, I just think that UF needs saving and I care enough to try. Therefore, I’ve developed a cunning plan: I’m going to buy four more copies of this book. The first I’ll send to Jeanine Frost because she was the first of my favorite UF authors to disappoint me this year. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hot wax? So not cool! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’ll send the second book to Chloe Neill, though I’m afraid she may already be beyond all hope. The remaining two copies have to be sent to the queen bee herself, our very own Charlaine Harris. She needs to read one and swallow the other like a medicine. Hell, I might even go wild and send a fifth copy to Patricia Briggs, because let’s face it, River Marked really wasn’t all that! <br /><br />Amazing, amazing, amazing! That’s pretty much all I can say about this book. I especially love that there’s some Slavic mythology thrown into the mix. <br /><br />Kate aka bunnycakes and her sugar woogums, His Furriness (hey, her words, not mine) are in a world of trouble… again! A secret society known as the Lighthouse Keepers hired a crazy scientist. He's building a device that can wipe out all magic within a four-mile radius. Life without magic isn’t easy for most of our characters, but the much bigger problem is that the device also kills every single magical person. That means the Pack, the People, witches, mages and just about everybody else. It’s basically an atomic bomb for the magical community. <br />In addition to that, the Beast Lord and his Consort (who hates to be called Mate) have other problems: Kate finds out the truth about her mother, which brings out a series of very difficult questions regarding her relationship with Curran, Andrea’s retired and not at all herself, a very important person gets mortally wounded, the boudas are creating more trouble than they’re worth and there’s even a pregnant Alpha in the Keep. <br /><br />Favorite quote:<br /><i>I could've fallen for someone steady. Dependable. Well-grounded. But nooo, I had to lose my head over this idiot.</i><br /><br />After all that, the only thing left to say is: Go read this book. Now! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9123918237605038137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2945264640170810232">Yes I am reading this again....3rd time is a charm. I even found some lovely people to read it with me at <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148835-ilona-andrews-addicts-iaa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ilona Andrews Addicts (IAA)</a>
</b><br/><br/>I always find something in these books that I missed or forgot in-between reads that makes them great and new again. Always a fun time reading the banter, the story and just the feel of IA's worlds are fantastic.<br/><br/><br/><b>Read #2 review Sept 2014</b><br/><br/>4.5 stars.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/best_zps254aa930.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText2945264640170810232" style="display:none">Yes I am reading this again....3rd time is a charm. I even found some lovely people to read it with me at <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148835-ilona-andrews-addicts-iaa" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilona Andrews Addicts (IAA)</a>
</b><br><br>I always find something in these books that I missed or forgot in-between reads that makes them great and new again. Always a fun time reading the banter, the story and just the feel of IA's worlds are fantastic.<br><br><br><b>Read #2 review Sept 2014</b><br><br>4.5 stars.<br><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/best_zps254aa930.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

My real review is below this is just me fangirling.<br><br><i>“I've been assigned to bodyguard you."<br>You've got to be kidding me.<br>Derek snorted.<br>Ascanio pretended not to hear it. "The Beast Lord spoke to me this morning. I'm responsible for your well-being, and if you get injured, I'll answer to him personally."<br>Oh, that bastard. Found the kid an impossible job, did he?<br>Derek laughed quietly.<br>Ascanio finally deemed it necessary to acknowledge Derek's existence. "Is something funny?"<br>"I don't even know you, and I feel sorry for you.”</i><br><br><b>Kate you are the freaking best. You and your crazy mutant attack poodle.</b><br><br><i>“I came to the table, pulled up a chair, and sat. <br>“Everyone brought a pet. I feel left out.” <br>An enthusiastic howl broke the silence, and Grendel bounded through the doorway. </a><br><br>It’s all rainbows, unicorns and glitter.<br><br><i>“Andrea raised her hand. “This is the hand that slapped Aunt B.”<br>“Maybe you should have it gold-plated.”<br>“Here, you can touch it, since you’re my best friend.”</i><br><br><b>I forgot how freaking hilarious Saiman is.</b><br><br><i>“Did he just rip out the engine?" I asked.<br>"Yes", Saiman said. "And now he is demolishing the Maserati with it."<br>Ten seconds later Curran hurled the twisted wreck of black and orange that used to be the Maserati into the wall.<br>The first melodic notes of an old song came from the computer. I glanced at Saiman.<br>He shrugged. "It begged for a soundtrack.”</i><br><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/sunshine_zps14ebbbed.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>^ Me the rest of the day.<br><br>And finally my favorite scene was…..<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“If I fought for them and was crippled, they would all say nice things,and then they would replace me and forget I was ever there. You would stay with me. You would take care of me, because you love me. I love you too, Kate. If you ever became hurt, I would not leave you.<br>I’ll be there. Wherever you want ‘there’ to be.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><br><b>Real Coherent Review from Sept 29 2013 </b><br><br>Possible minor spoilers books 1-4<br><br>Kate and Curran are finally together as a couple and that means she is struggling to learn what it is to be not only a member of a pack but also half in charge of it. Kate is also trying to get her business that the pack fronted the money for up and going. So far it isn’t going well until a case lands in her lap.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Rene, you want us to find you-don't-know-who and to retrieve his you-don't-know-what for you-won't-tell-me-whom?”</i>
</b><br><br>Well at least it is a job. With the help of Andrea and Derek, Kate is off and running with it. But it seems the you-don’t-know-what part of the job might just in fact destroy the magical community. There are brand new witches and warlocks, more unusual mythology along with revelations from Kate’s past that lead her to question everything about the man she thought of as her father.<br><br>Many of our favorite characters are back, the boy wonder Derek, Julie, Saiman, Aunt B and Andrea of course as well as one of my new favorites Barabas the were-mongoose. Nanny/adviser to Kate he is trying to help her become more like the alpha for the pack she needs to be.<br><br><b>
  <i>“I know it's late, but could you find a book for me? It's called The Slavs: Study of Pagan Tradition by Osvintsev."<br>Barabas sighed dramatically. "Kate, you make me despair. Let's try that again from the top, except this time pretend you are an alpha."<br>"I don't need a lecture. I just need the book."<br>"Much better. Little more growl in the voice?"<br>"Barabas!"<br>"And we're there. Congratulations!”</i>
</b><br><br>There are again some heart wrenching choices to be made and humungous obstacles to overcome. I really liked the plot of this book and the interactions of course between Curran and Kate. Both are so broken in some respects but always fiercely loyal and overprotective of one another. <br><br><b>
  <i>“Yes I can,” Curran snarled. “Listen: this is me telling you what you will not do.”<br>I raised the cookbook and tapped him on the nose. ”Bad cat.”</i>
</b><br><br> Kate really comes into her own in some respects in this book. She takes charge and doesn’t back down from a fight no matter if it is in the council room, with Curran or against her newest enemy. She has to deal with some of her insecurities steeping from being alone for so long and not knowing how to depend on and trust others around her. <br><br>Magic Slays is another good book in the series showing Kate getting stronger so that ultimately she can face her biological father. In each book she has picked up another piece of her power and that is true of this one too. But it seems that the odds will still be insurmountable if she ever comes face to face with the man who gave her life. It will be interesting to see how the authors come up with a believable ending to the series but I’m sure with everything they have put into this it will be fantastic. <br><br><br><br>Sept 29, 2013<br><br>But just a quick question for the other Kate Daniels lovers. In the first few books Kate is supposed to be careful who she has sex with because there can be some sort of transference of power through sex<br><br>But that doesn't appear to be happening. Unless now it has just changed to someone using her power because she loves them. Or are they still using protection and so condoms also protect against magical transfers as well. <br><br>Anyone else get caught up on that or just me?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-library-catalogue">my-library-catalogue</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785656240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6608290615025888055">I now count myself among the Kate Daniels super fandom. Magic Slays was another great installment on what is shaping up to be an awesome series. Since I’ve gushed about it enough in other reviews, I’ll stick to specifics for this title. I especially loved how authentic the relationship was between the main character and her bff. They argued like real people, and it’s the kind of back-and-forth bickering that’s fun to read about. In fact, all the relationships are great, and I especially love how</span>
  <span id="freeText6608290615025888055" style="display:none">I now count myself among the Kate Daniels super fandom. Magic Slays was another great installment on what is shaping up to be an awesome series. Since I’ve gushed about it enough in other reviews, I’ll stick to specifics for this title. I especially loved how authentic the relationship was between the main character and her bff. They argued like real people, and it’s the kind of back-and-forth bickering that’s fun to read about. In fact, all the relationships are great, and I especially love how many interesting side characters get their own spotlights in some of the short stories (yup – it’s good enough to read all of the extra novellas that go along with it!). I’ll probably be doing a Kate Daniels short story blitz once I get through them all.<br /><br />Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.nikihawkes.com</a> </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169726026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8804961929801084353">Coming off the high of the spectacular ending of <i>Magic Slays</i>, I've been staring at the computer for 10 minutes, trying to figure out why it took me a little while to really get into this book. And I think I've finally come up with the answer.<br/><br/>As the story begins, Kate is running the new agency that Curran set up for her since she has left the Order. But despite her competence and reputation, she doesn't have any clients. But just as her best friend Andrea returns from a two month absence, Kate is</span>
  <span id="freeText8804961929801084353" style="display:none">Coming off the high of the spectacular ending of <i>Magic Slays</i>, I've been staring at the computer for 10 minutes, trying to figure out why it took me a little while to really get into this book. And I think I've finally come up with the answer.<br /><br />As the story begins, Kate is running the new agency that Curran set up for her since she has left the Order. But despite her competence and reputation, she doesn't have any clients. But just as her best friend Andrea returns from a two month absence, Kate is hired to find a missing man and the mysterious device he has built. She investigates; she is snarky; she is magic and bad-ass. But (insert light bulb here) I wasn't very invested in any of it, because Kate seemed to have no stake in it all, beyond completing a job. No justice mission like she had when searching for Greg's killer; no revenge for a brutal attack on a friend; no saving the world from a deranged aunt. Just a job.<br /><br />It was when Kate realized what the device could do and what it would mean to her world, that I began to perk up. And then we were off and running. Without spoiling too much, I'll say that the device could have huge ramifications on Kate and all those she loves, if it is activated. And as we get into the second half of the book, Kate encounters a personal crisis, that makes her willing to risk everything to fix it. It's when Kate is desperate and loyal and determined that she is at her best. And here she shines, a heroine in the greatest sense.<br /><br />Curran is back as Kate's mate, and I was worried that some of the spark would be missing from their relationship, now that it's more permanent. But Kate's paranoia keeps them from falling into the old-married couple routine. She still has questions about whether things can work for them long-term. But as the story progresses, he proves himself to be an utterly worthy hero. And I still enjoyed the fire between them.<br /><br />For the last third of the book, I was completely unable to put it down. The ending was fantastic and sets up even more drama for the next installment. I can't imagine that Kate will be able to keep her secret for much longer. 4 1/2 stars.<br /><br /><i>*ARC Provided by Penguin Group USA</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8804961929801084353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1075796854" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1075796854" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1075796854?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1075796854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14222009400566648386">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina' rel='nofollow noopener'>Armina</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17237503-eilonwy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eilonwy</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asya</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Monty Cupcake</a>.<br/><br/>Poor Kate Daniels opened a private investigation outfit quite a while ago, but the clients did not exactly form a huge line at her doors. In fact she did not have a single one yet. When her friend/enemy Ghastek asked her to deal with a vampire on the loose she jumped at the chance. Before she knew it, the little problem escalates into something much bigger. She now has to deal with pissed off police, her adopted niece Julie who disappeared</span>
  <span id="freeText14222009400566648386" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina" rel="nofollow noopener">Armina</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17237503-eilonwy" rel="nofollow noopener">Eilonwy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya" rel="nofollow noopener">Asya</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake" rel="nofollow noopener">Monty Cupcake</a>.<br /><br />Poor Kate Daniels opened a private investigation outfit quite a while ago, but the clients did not exactly form a huge line at her doors. In fact she did not have a single one yet. When her friend/enemy Ghastek asked her to deal with a vampire on the loose she jumped at the chance. Before she knew it, the little problem escalates into something much bigger. She now has to deal with pissed off police, her adopted niece Julie who disappeared, and accept a very questionable assignment from an elite guard unit called Red Guards. Kate's life became anything but boring.<br /><br />In my opinion this was the second best book of the series after Magic Strikes. It has its own share of problems, but the positive parts overweight negative ones by far. The things I do not like include the following.<br /><br />The authors missed a chance to show a very interesting battle with a bridge troll. We are shown Kate rushing in, the next scene start with a description of the aftermath. Was it the desire to keep the number of pages low which influenced this?<br /><br />I realized I do not care about Julie. I understand that she is 15-year-old girl - and we all know what is means - but I do not find a <b>single</b> redeeming quality in her at all. I really could not care less what would happen to her. She is a failure as an interesting character.<br /><br />The ending felt rushed and the resolution felt kind of on the easy side, but when you think about it, this was the most logical thing what would happen as the forces in the fight were nowhere near being equal.<br /><br />In the good parts I liked the appearance of some very colorful characters from Slavic (Eastern Slavic?) folklore. I did not expect for Baba Yaga to appear the way she was described here, but let us call it artistic liberty.<br /><br />The biggest reason for high rating was a moral of the story. The humanity created myths for as long as we can recall; some of them were very ingenious, some quite gruesome, some quite entertaining. Despite this, we - the humans - <b>have yet to come up</b> with a creature/monster/god/entity more dangerous than a bunch of fanatics in real life. Our collective imagination is not up to the task, simple as that. I said it was a moral, but at no point in the story this became preachy, or hammered relentlessly. Well done, dear authors!<br /><br />The plot was entertaining and fast-moving. Everything taken together constitutes a solid 4-star rating. <br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my BookLikes one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gene.booklikes.com/post/1013815/during-all-of-it-history-the-humans-could-not-come-up-with-scarier-monsters-than-real-life-fanatics">http://gene.booklikes.com/post/101381...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14222009400566648386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6543141308937452402" style="display:none">I am continually amazed by how this series just gets better and better with every book. Illona Andrews is a fantastic writing team. In this Kate DAniels adventure, something is causing various players in the magical world to act weird all of a sudden, and no one can figure out why. Of course, Kate is hired to source out the problem and the complications that ensue are some of the most exciting so far. <br /><br />I love the relationships in these books, and those were featured here. Curran and Kate are absolutely my favorites, but I also love the friendships that exist, and getting those Derek, Andrea, Dolittle, Jim, etc moments really make the books for me.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[... one of the most interesting things to me was the story line involving Julie going lupe and Kate having to use her blood to save her. Having Julie become one of the shapeshifters not only changes things in an interesting way, but also inserted that real human angle.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Please excuse typos.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110803941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10052339302231167800">The fifth book in the <i>Kate Daniels</i> Series, <b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> is just as <b>AMAZING</b> as all the rest. <i>Ilona Andrews</i> is one of my all-time favorite authors and I am so amazed at how with each book in the Kate Daniels series I grow closer and closer to these characters that I have so much emotion welled up in me. Yes. I cried like a big baby. That is how great and close you come to love these characters. You think of them as real and you adore each and everyone of them.<br/><br/><b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> is the book! Yes, the book </span>
  <span id="freeText10052339302231167800" style="display:none">The fifth book in the <i>Kate Daniels</i> Series, <b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> is just as <b>AMAZING</b> as all the rest. <i>Ilona Andrews</i> is one of my all-time favorite authors and I am so amazed at how with each book in the Kate Daniels series I grow closer and closer to these characters that I have so much emotion welled up in me. Yes. I cried like a big baby. That is how great and close you come to love these characters. You think of them as real and you adore each and everyone of them.<br /><br /><b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> is the book! Yes, the book where we get to see how Kate and Curran are as a couple, not just as a couple, but as Beast Lord and Consort. Kate and Curran were just as wonderful in this book as they were in the others. And yes, for those who will be begging to know, there is more Kate and Curran in <b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> and all I have to say is after this book, I want to steal Curran for myself. He makes my heart beat like crazy.<br /><br /><em>
  <b> ""Laugh while you can. You have to sleep eventually, and then I'll take my revenge." "You're such a violent woman. Always with the threats. You should look into some meditation techniques..."</b>
</em><br /><br />I had to stop myself from skimming through the book for all of the Kate and Curran scenes. I have a serious Kate and Curran addiction and I don't want help. Their scenes together were absolute perfection. And we really do see how much Curran cares about Kate. Aww...ummm..Kate do you mind if I steal him away from you? I love him.<br /><br /><em>
  <b> "Jealous of the actors now, are we?"<br />"What, of some fancy boy on the screen? Inconceivable."<br />Oh, this was going to be good.</b>
</em><br /><br />So Kate is Consort to the Beast Lord and I bet you are all wondering how she is doing at that. She is so bad ass. Even though Curran tells Kate what to do she won't take any of that shit. haha. Just the way I like Kate. I adored Kate in this book. There are some things that we get to learn about Kate's past that she didn't even know and it made me tear up a bit, but that's because I love her.<br /><br />As Consort, Kate does have a little power and there's this one scene in <b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> where I am like <b>"Best Kate Daniels Showdown EVER!</b> You Go, Girl!" We do get some surprises along the way that I will not spill, but it made me go <b>WHAT?! HUH?! and YEAH!</b> A lot of crazy emotions all at once. Characters that I worried about, laughed and cried with and you will too.<br /><br /><b>MAGIC SLAYS</b> does not disappoint. Look forward to having your butt glued to your seat(like Curran glued Kate's butt to her chair in <i>Magic Bleeds</i> LOL) all day while enjoying yet another astounding book in the <i>Kate Daniels</i> Series</span>
  <a data-text-id="10052339302231167800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
