        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995982824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9716934826552125320"><b> First read July 2014<br/>Second read May 2016</b><br/><br/>This time this book was even better. There were so many things I had forgotten, I didn't remember all the vohlv/witches/Adam situations. <br/><br/>But as you know, I have real issues with the relationship between Kate and Curran. Many of my questions were answered. But before that, these were the hints that made me doubt all the feelings between them. When I say between, I mean on Curran's part, because I know Kate adores him.<br/><br/><br/><i>“All those years, all those women, and </i></span>
  <span id="freeText9716934826552125320" style="display:none"><b> First read July 2014<br />Second read May 2016</b><br /><br />This time this book was even better. There were so many things I had forgotten, I didn't remember all the vohlv/witches/Adam situations. <br /><br />But as you know, I have real issues with the relationship between Kate and Curran. Many of my questions were answered. But before that, these were the hints that made me doubt all the feelings between them. When I say between, I mean on Curran's part, because I know Kate adores him.<br /><br /><br /><i>“All those years, all those women, and you are the one he mated with. He was interested in more than your bed, I can tell you that.”<br /><br />..........................<br /><br />“-that you’ve chained yourself to this man who seeks only to further his own interests at the expense of your feelings and safety, and that his careless use of your power has drawn the attention of your father.”<br /><br />...........................<br /><br />“One way or the other, the clash between Roland and the Pack was coming. What did Curran have to lose by mating with me?”</i><br /><br /><br />You see, with all these, how can I believe in Curran's honesty? I see the things as they are. A war is coming and Curran has the best weapon to confront Roland. <br /><br />I got my answers about this. I get to see what Curran thinks about the pack and the war, and I liked him for what he said, but then BOOK #6 happened and I was back to disliking him. <br /><br />This book was more about Kate and her relationships with the people who helped her growing up. I felt so sorry for her and all the things that her stepfather made her do. <br /><br /><br /><i>“My whole childhood was a lie. Even Voron’s thirst for vengeance wasn’t real. It was implanted in him when my mother’s magic had seared his brain."<br /><br />.........................<br /><br />“All of it was so when my father and I met, we could kill each other, and Voron would have the last laugh.”<br /><br />..........................<br /><br /> <br />“I was the biological by-product of a megalomaniac and a woman who magically brainwashed others into doing her will, and I was raised by a man who reveled in the knowledge that my biological father would one day kill me.”</i><br /><br />Of course I would like things to have been different, but all those made her powerful and fearless. Kate is a very special woman who deserves the best. ( cough *Hugh* cough) :P<br /><br />The book felt a bit dark, so many deaths. My heart broke for Julie. The scenes where Derek stands by her are so beautiful. Kate's thoughts and feelings for her made me cry. That's pure love. <br /><br />Despite this, the humour is never absent. The confrontation between Evdokia and Gregorii is priceless.<br /><br />This book has the best ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Hugh congratulating Kate and sending her flowers.... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> * swoons * <br />If that is not romantic, then I don't know what romance is. <br /><br />I'm not ready for book #6, I'll never be. :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="9716934826552125320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Imagine the horror if one of those mindless monsters were to break free of their handler’s </span>
  <span id="freeText17633232955224297586" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484947887i/21770756._SX540_.jpg" width="462" height="305.2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>(Am I ever going to get tired of posting Kraft Dinner images in these reviews you may be asking???….. <i>probably,</i> but not quite yet.)<br><br>In Kate’s Atlanta, much to my fang-gritting annoyance, vampires are vessels of pure bloodlust without any sentience of their own, they require ‘handlers’ to move about with any agenda other than ripping their fangs through everything that finds itself in their path. Imagine the horror if one of those mindless monsters were to break free of their handler’s mind control? <b>Utter chaos.</b> <br><br>So begins <u>Magic Slays</u>. ..<br><br>There is a lot of change going on in Kate’s life in this one; navigating a new relationship, trying to rein in her street-savvy teenage ward, the start-up of her new business. There’s lots happening here, guys and ghouls, even outside of the actual mystery itself. <br><br>We get to see some of Kate’s insecurities in this one (which is a refreshing change) as well as learning a little bit more about why you don’t want to fuck around with the Beast Lord. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I personally wouldn’t be so forgiving of his <i>little</i> car throwing fit of jealousy. I still found the actual language used in this story questionable but the meat of the story more than made up for it this time around. <br><br>The Big Bads in <u>Magic Slays</u> are of an entirely different nature, one that is more feasibly horrifying to me. We get introduced to a new teenaged bouda who’s libido gets him in some trouble but whom I think I am going to grow to like quite a bit. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And it has to be said that the scene where Kate comes on Ascanio’s broken body protecting Julie was endearing as fuck! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483478736i/21616763._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13561660678717838695"><b>
  <i><br/>"Emotional scars never heal completely. You’ll never recover.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>I once mentioned that UF reviews is the hardest for me, so far things haven't changed. I have no idea why I find it hard to review them, this is the best I could come up with at the moment, I know it definitely won't do justice to this book.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Put your badass faces on and follow me.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>The one thing that this book lack is romance, it didn't get enough page space as I wanted, given the fact that the ship has finally sailed. Apart fr</span>
  <span id="freeText13561660678717838695" style="display:none"><b>
  <i><br />"Emotional scars never heal completely. You’ll never recover.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />I once mentioned that UF reviews is the hardest for me, so far things haven't changed. I have no idea why I find it hard to review them, this is the best I could come up with at the moment, I know it definitely won't do justice to this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Put your badass faces on and follow me.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The one thing that this book lack is romance, it didn't get enough page space as I wanted, given the fact that the ship has finally sailed. Apart from that everything in this book is superb.<br /><br />We got non stop action, a plot to die for and characters to kill for.<br /><br />All the old gang are back with one additional Ascanio a teenage bouda, he is a worse, more reckless, and handsome version of Raphael, I loved his character development so much.<br /><br />Derek, Jim, Julie, Andrea and Curran were all in this. I loved that Andrea and Kate are together once again, but I hate the circumstance that made it happened.<br /><br />Curran is a better mate than I anticipated, I was expecting a control and over protective freak but got a loving and compromising Curran, what could be more better than this.<br /><br />Kate is the same but somehow better, been with Curran didn't make her dependent, she is still independent but now she accepts helps, she so deserve him and all her friends.</span>

They suck me in. <br>And I'm having sweet problems with navigating through all these sequels and novellas and Curran POV's. <br><br>I love music and obviously, I love books, so those two love often come together. <br>Reading this series, I was listening to a lot of Evanescence. <br><br>Book one and two very confusing, books three and four love it...this one still good, still riding that wave....of awesomeness. <br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507851189ra/24156541.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Bring on all the rest of the books! <div id="review_550569010" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550569010?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11055258-magic-slays">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550569010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5225947722839490051">February 2018 Reread.<br/>August 2016 re-read: JFC. This book - had me on the edge of tears for nearly 60% of it (possibly more). I love this series. I love the humor and how the stakes are high - and not everyone always makes it, so you learn to cherish the moments as they happen. But damn. It rips my heart out sometimes.<br/><br/>And that ending. The note. The flowers! O_o<br/><br/>September 2015 re-read: This book easily ties for my favorite of the series - but with so many excellent books in this series it's still h</span>
  <span id="freeText5225947722839490051" style="display:none">February 2018 Reread.<br />August 2016 re-read: JFC. This book - had me on the edge of tears for nearly 60% of it (possibly more). I love this series. I love the humor and how the stakes are high - and not everyone always makes it, so you learn to cherish the moments as they happen. But damn. It rips my heart out sometimes.<br /><br />And that ending. The note. The flowers! O_o<br /><br />September 2015 re-read: This book easily ties for my favorite of the series - but with so many excellent books in this series it's still hard to choose. I love it.<br /><br />20 July 2014: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004LRPJ72/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B004LRPJ72&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=touthenig-20&amp;linkId=V5D3XE4BXXV46W2B" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Kindle</a><br /><br />Review (sort of):<br />I plan to do a full review of this later - these are just my quick thoughts.<br /><br />I loved it!! Ilona Andrews just continues to blow me away with their stories. It's such a deep, vivid, layered world with complex characters around every corner.<br /><br />I liked the reality of Kate starting her own business. Of having partners/employees. The difficulties and issues that come with that and how she handled them. <br /><br />The growth and development in Kate and Curran's relationship is fantastic. This isn't just an HEA, ride off into the sunset; this is an HEA in progress (to steal Ilona's words). There are hurdles still to be overcome, trust still to be issues, secrets still to be discussed, and compromises to be made. I'm confident in their HEA, I know they'll never falter, never give up on one another and never let each other go...but it still takes effort for both of them at times. I like that we see that. Also the issues with Kate being the other half of the Alpha pair. There's some politics that take place in this book, and all I can say is I was cheering for Kate when she was done. Loved the way she handled a very tense situation.<br /><br />The action of the storyline is intense. What starts as a job quickly becomes possibly the biggest threat that Kate has faced yet. <br /><br />There are some mind-blowing bits of Kate's history revealed in this book. I'm still trying to wrap my head around them, and decide what to take at face value and what to dig a little deeper on.<br /><br />In addition to this, there's the trademark humor, smart-assedness and absolutely heart-wrenching moments. I laughed out loud more times than I can count, and teared up just as often.<br /><br />The last few chapters of the book are a wild roller-coaster of a ride, that I'm going to be reading again right now for what I'm sure I missed.<br /><br />All in all, great book, great story. Must read and I highly recommend this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5225947722839490051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_166445177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166445177" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166445177?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kate Daniels fans, UF fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166445177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14648500191666445475">I'm a fan of the Kate Daniels series, and recently I was looking for a guaranteed re-read. It wasn't too long before <u>Magic Slays</u> caught my eye, especially as the next book in the series is coming out at the end of July (and probably because I shelve my books alphabetically). Now past the giddy first and second reads, it is time for a thorough review. Fans of the series won't be disappointed by its action-packed story, continued world-building, and trademark humor, but I miss the finesse of earli</span>
  <span id="freeText14648500191666445475" style="display:none">I'm a fan of the Kate Daniels series, and recently I was looking for a guaranteed re-read. It wasn't too long before <u>Magic Slays</u> caught my eye, especially as the next book in the series is coming out at the end of July (and probably because I shelve my books alphabetically). Now past the giddy first and second reads, it is time for a thorough review. Fans of the series won't be disappointed by its action-packed story, continued world-building, and trademark humor, but I miss the finesse of earlier books.<br /><br />For me and my sketchy memory, its always worth noting when the jacket blurb gets it wrong--this time by essentially summarizing the first twenty pages. My own non-spoiler synopsis would be a little more comprehensive: "Andrea returns after a two month disappearance, and before long, she and Kate are investigating a kidnapping for Rene of the Red Guard. A successful case for the Guards could make Kate's career. However, the investigation is complicated by several seemingly random instances of magic disappearing. Tracking the solution down will take require connecting the Russian volhvs, who seem to be involved, and with Atlanta's witches. At the same time, Kate is struggling with negotiating her relationship to Curran, her role in the Pack, and how to safely raise Julie in an unsafe world. Kate and her loved ones are about to face one of the greatest threats to their existence."<br /><br />Now, the analysis. It took me until the third read to analyze it, but this book feels lacking in the finesse of the earlier ones. I know, I know; subtle may not be the term you think of with UF, but this one felt more extreme, the kickbocking version versus fencing. The emotions are dynamic. The conflict is extreme, and written in a way that starts to feel a little like sermonizing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ There's more than one instance of someone explaining to Kate "why a small group of people would want to kill everyone else," including Dolittle, Curran and Saiman. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The relationship dramas are bold. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She does the existential "why would he want me" debate, made worse by taking to the witch  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The reveals for Kate fundamentally alter her concept of her own history. Certain events are life-shattering. While some of these concerns are plotting and others characterization, I feel like Andrews usually smooths them better, with appropriate transitions applied and maybe a shade less drama.<br /><br />I also have to admit that Curran is fairly close to insufferable in this book. Again, I understand; he's the leader of a group of shapeshifters, he has to control his own enormous power, etc. However, he's very controlling of Kate's behavior, manipulative and conditional. What do I mean? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The office bordering vampire territory being a surprise to Kate. Dropping the petitions on her. Pushing her to allow Julie to stay with the Pack. Giving her Derek and Ascanio. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Just when it seems Kate has stood her ground, he changes his mind after extensive healthy discussion <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (specifically, the blood transference scene when he says, "If you think that I will every let you pull that fucked-up shit again, then this thing between you and me is done. We are fucking done)."  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> If that isn't a hallmark statement of an controlling partner, then I don't know what is. That final scene pushed my sense of balance between them over the edge.<br /><br />From my behind the scenes readings of the Andrews blog, they intended to write a book that ramps up both action and consequences. I can commend that as a series arc, and think they manage to do that well while still resolving major plot arcs within each book. However, some of it felt a little forced, a little contrived and didn't quite work for me. One of the obvious oddities was Andrea leaving the kids. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why would Kate keep Julie at the office at all, when her whole stress was about keeping her safe? Why would Andrea leave the kids knowing a loose vampire had just been there recently? It seemed more necessary for moving events forward than internally consistent. I was also surprised at how many people were killed by the magic bomb when it's only been a few generations since magic hit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> A small point that to me illustrates the extremism: all the males are physically enormously attractive--Rapheal, Ascanio, Barabas, the Russian mage. Its an example of the concept of exceptionalism of all the characters, the larger-than-life perspective of the soap opera mentality. Oh, and one more small oddity--Kate is told that the Pack has a library-- "both paper and digital." Um? Is it me, or is that incongruent?<br /><br />As usual, there were a few marvelously absurd laughs including knitting vampires and pretty much all the encounters with the Russian mages:<br />"'Oh, Is that so?' He raised his hand to his goatee.<br />That does it. 'Yeah. And what's with the beard and the horse mane? You look like Rent-a-Villain.'<br />The volhv's eyes widened. He waved his hand at me. 'Well you don't look... female... in your pants.'<br />"That''s a hell of an insult. Did you think of it all by yourself or did you have to ask your god for help?"<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, it's an action packed book that kept me planted on the couch, reading until I reached the end. The mystery Kate begins investigating with Andrea is an interesting puzzle. Once again, it was fun meeting new magical types and having them re-interpreted. I did appreciate that the relationship between Kate and Curran avoided the stereotypical "hothead" reaction of the misunderstanding and stomp-off until dramatic reconciliation (although they are doing that with Andrea and Rapheal). Overall, although it isn't my favorite in the series, its still far more entertaining than most of the female UF out there.<br /><br /><br />Cross-posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/06/06/magic-slays-by-ilona-andrews/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14648500191666445475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" href="/user/show/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun">Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588347602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16880499145220099627">It's no secret anymore that I'm madly in love with Kate and that I'd totally marry her. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8559047.Magic_Slays__Kate_Daniels___5_' title='Magic Slays (Kate Daniels, #5) by Ilona Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magic Slays</a> is another favorite book of mine in her series because it is action packed, fast paced and has <br/><br/><b>Sarcasm</b><br/><i>I did some thinking.” “That is a very dangerous pastime,” Ghastek said. He’d made a joke. Surely the apocalypse wasn’t far behind.</i><br/><br/><b>A lovely character cast</b><br/><i>I nodded to the boy wonder and the sex fiend.</i><br/><br/>Derek, Ascanio, Jim, Saiman, Aunt B. ... They are all part of the party again. <br/><br/><b>Fun politics</b><br/><i>Kate, it’</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16880499145220099627" style="display:none">It's no secret anymore that I'm madly in love with Kate and that I'd totally marry her. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8559047.Magic_Slays__Kate_Daniels___5_" title="Magic Slays (Kate Daniels, #5) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Slays</a> is another favorite book of mine in her series because it is action packed, fast paced and has <br /><br /><b>Sarcasm</b><br /><i>I did some thinking.” “That is a very dangerous pastime,” Ghastek said. He’d made a joke. Surely the apocalypse wasn’t far behind.</i><br /><br /><b>A lovely character cast</b><br /><i>I nodded to the boy wonder and the sex fiend.</i><br /><br />Derek, Ascanio, Jim, Saiman, Aunt B. ... They are all part of the party again. <br /><br /><b>Fun politics</b><br /><i>Kate, it’s not personal. It’s protocol and it’s common sense. You don’t challenge people under you, you don’t get to skip formal dinners, and when you go to see an unstable coward who screwed half of Atlanta and propositioned you in public, you bring an escort. Deal with it.</i><br /><br /><b>Philosophy</b><br /><i>Rage is a powerful thing. People get upset over many things. Frustrating jobs, small paychecks, bad hours. People want things; people feel humiliated by others who have the things they want; people feel deprived and powerless. All this gives fuel to rage. The anger builds and builds and if there is no outlet for it, pretty soon it transforms the person. They walk around like a loaded gun, ready to go off if only they could find the right target. They want to hurt something. They need it.</i><br /><br /><b>Romance</b><br /><i>Curran growled. “Later, babycakes.” Babycakes. Asshole. “Good hunting, sugar woogums.”</i><br /><br />Speed re read at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148835-ilona-andrews-addicts-iaa" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilona Andrews Addicts</a> because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17333174.Magic_Binds__Kate_Daniels___9_" title="Magic Binds (Kate Daniels, #9) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Binds</a> will be released on September 20th *faints*</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1l56BPSFNRYuzpYGOUGrWeTLkADA4YYGfIu/TAtNSKs+2g2Fb30jofLvQmj5PDTrghvFxBgmU0kqgqL5b1WdJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FgZVXw4oWGK2ZqwygiKaN+Z5MF825GCnyAD8IOmDbMr+giLeldBO1WpHeFxCXwWFgKllm+4jteieCeGVjZu5Rg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer530995616140910757">Ilona Andrews is the pseudonym for a husband-and-wife writing team. Ilona is a native-born Russian and Gordon is a former communications sergeant in the U.S. Army. Contrary to popular belief, Gordon was never an intelligence officer with a license to kill, and Ilona was never the mysterious Russian spy who seduced him. They met in college, in English Composition 101, where Ilona got a better grade</span>
  <span id="freeText530995616140910757" style="display:none">Ilona Andrews is the pseudonym for a husband-and-wife writing team. Ilona is a native-born Russian and Gordon is a former communications sergeant in the U.S. Army. Contrary to popular belief, Gordon was never an intelligence officer with a license to kill, and Ilona was never the mysterious Russian spy who seduced him. They met in college, in English Composition 101, where Ilona got a better grade. (Gordon is still sore about that.)<br /><br />Gordon and Ilona currently reside in Oregon with their two children, three dogs and a cat. They have co-authored two series, the bestselling urban fantasy of Kate Daniels and romantic urban fantasy of The Edge.<br /></span>
